Second Proof: Direction Implies Motion or Rest
Sanusi's second proof: direction requires motion or rest.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Sanusi's second argument that being in a direction would subject God to motion or rest, both of which are originated, leading to origination.

Core Idea
Direction forces motion or rest; both are created, so God cannot be in a direction.

Sanusi offers a second argument: anything that is in a direction cannot be free from either moving within that direction or remaining still. Both motion and rest are originated (hadith) attributes—they come into existence. Therefore, whatever is subject to them must itself be originated. This would make God contingent, which is impossible.

Guided Path
1
Read the argument
Read the Arabic and translation. Notice the conditional structure: 'if in a direction, then not free from motion or rest.'
2
Understand the dichotomy
Recognize that motion and rest are opposites, but both are temporal events. Sanusi uses the principle 'whatever cannot be free from originated things is itself originated.'
3
Apply to God
Since God is eternal and uncreated, He cannot be subject to originated states. Therefore, He cannot be in a direction.
4
Reflect on the logic
This is an example of 'burhan al-tatbiq' or the argument from incompatibility. Consider why motion and rest are considered originated.
In kalam, any change or state that begins is originated.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عوارض البطن ، وخلف مِنْ عوارضِ الظَّهِرِ ، وَمَنِ استحال عليهِ أنْ يكونَ جِرْماً .. استحالَ أَنْ يَتَصفَ بهذهِ الأعضاءِ ولوازمها على الضرورة . قوله : ( لأنَّهُ لا يعمرُها إلا الأجرام ) يعني : لأنَّ شغل الجهةِ يستلزم التحيز ، وكلُّ مُتحيّر فهو جزمٌ ، والله عزَّ وجلَّ يستحيل أن يكونَ جِرْماً ، ولأنَّهُ لو كانَ في جهةٍ لكانَ إِمَّا أكبر منها وإِمَّا أصغر (۱) ويحتاج إلى المخصص (۲) وأيضاً : فلو كانَ في جهةٍ لم يخلُ : إما أن يتحرَّكَ فيها أو يسكن ، وكلٌّ مِنَ الحركة والسكونِ حادث ، فما لا يخلو عنهما حادث وأيضاً : فلو كانَ في جهةٍ لاحتاجَ إِلى مَنْ يُخصِّصُهُ بجهةٍ دونَ جهة ، وذلك يستلزم الحدوث
The accidents of the belly, and the throat from the accidents of the back, and whoever it is impossible for him to be a body, it is impossible for him to be described with these organs and their necessary concomitants necessarily. His saying: (Because only bodies occupy them) means: because occupying direction necessitates occupying space, and everything that occupies space is a body, and Allah, exalted and magnificent, is impossible to be a body. And because if He were in a direction, He would either be larger than it or smaller (1) and would need a determinant (2). Also: if He were in a direction, it would not be free from either moving in it or being still, and both motion and rest are originated, so that which is not free from both is originated. Also: if He were in a direction, He would need one who specifies Him with a direction rather than another, and that necessitates origination.
Source pages p. 244

Commentary
This passage presents three proofs that God cannot be in a direction. First, Sanusi argues that occupying a direction entails being a body (jism), and God cannot be a body. Second, if God were in a direction, He would either be larger or smaller than that direction, requiring a determinant (mukhassis) to specify one size, which implies origination. Third, if in a direction, God would be subject to motion or rest, both of which are originated (hadith); thus what cannot be free of them is originated. The conclusion is that direction (jiha) is impossible for God.

Key Terms

حركة (haraka)
سكون (sukun)

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that God being in a direction does not force motion or rest—He could be static without change.
Correction: Rest (sukun) is still an originated state because it is a privation of motion that comes into being. Both are temporal.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi's second argument, what is true about both motion and rest?
A) They are eternal
B) They are originated
C) They are necessary
D) They are impossible for bodies

Key Takeaway
God cannot be in a direction because direction necessitates motion or rest, both of which are created attributes.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you truly believed that Allah is not confined to any direction, how would it change the way you think about His closeness to you when you pray? Is there a part of you that still imagines Him 'up there' in a literal sense? What would it take to internalize this truth such that your heart feels His presence without any spatial limitation?
?
The proof shows that direction forces motion or rest, both of which are created. Have you ever attributed to Allah a quality that actually belongs to created things, even unintentionally? How can you guard your heart from concepts that limit His transcendence?
?
This argument challenges the common imagination of God. When you find yourself picturing Allah in your mind, do you ever stop to correct that image? What concrete step will you take this week to ensure your conception of Allah is based on revelation and reason, not on human analogy?

Third Proof: Direction Requires a Determinant
Sanusi's third proof: direction needs a determinant.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Sanusi's third argument that being in a direction would require a determinant to specify which direction, indicating origination.

Core Idea
Direction needs a chooser; God needs no chooser, so He has no direction.

Sanusi presents a final argument: if God were in a direction, He would need someone or something to determine which direction He occupies. Any specification among possibilities requires a determinant (mukhassis), and the need for a determinant implies that the thing specified is originated. Since God is eternal and not subject to origination, He cannot be in a direction.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation. Note the phrase 'yukhasṣiṣuhu bi-jiha duna jiha' (specify Him with a direction rather than another).
2
Understand the principle of specification
In kalam, when something could be in multiple states, the actual state requires a determinant. This is a well-known argument.
3
Apply to God
If God were in a direction, there would be many possible directions. The actual one would need a cause to select it, making God dependent.
4
Conclude
Since God is self-sufficient and eternal, He cannot need a determinant. Thus, direction is impossible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عوارض البطن ، وخلف مِنْ عوارضِ الظَّهِرِ ، وَمَنِ استحال عليهِ أنْ يكونَ جِرْماً .. استحالَ أَنْ يَتَصفَ بهذهِ الأعضاءِ ولوازمها على الضرورة . قوله : ( لأنَّهُ لا يعمرُها إلا الأجرام ) يعني : لأنَّ شغل الجهةِ يستلزم التحيز ، وكلُّ مُتحيّر فهو جزمٌ ، والله عزَّ وجلَّ يستحيل أن يكونَ جِرْماً ، ولأنَّهُ لو كانَ في جهةٍ لكانَ إِمَّا أكبر منها وإِمَّا أصغر (۱) ويحتاج إلى المخصص (۲) وأيضاً : فلو كانَ في جهةٍ لم يخلُ : إما أن يتحرَّكَ فيها أو يسكن ، وكلٌّ مِنَ الحركة والسكونِ حادث ، فما لا يخلو عنهما حادث وأيضاً : فلو كانَ في جهةٍ لاحتاجَ إِلى مَنْ يُخصِّصُهُ بجهةٍ دونَ جهة ، وذلك يستلزم الحدوث
The accidents of the belly, and the throat from the accidents of the back, and whoever it is impossible for him to be a body, it is impossible for him to be described with these organs and their necessary concomitants necessarily. His saying: (Because only bodies occupy them) means: because occupying direction necessitates occupying space, and everything that occupies space is a body, and Allah, exalted and magnificent, is impossible to be a body. And because if He were in a direction, He would either be larger than it or smaller (1) and would need a determinant (2). Also: if He were in a direction, it would not be free from either moving in it or being still, and both motion and rest are originated, so that which is not free from both is originated. Also: if He were in a direction, He would need one who specifies Him with a direction rather than another, and that necessitates origination.
Source pages p. 244

Commentary
This passage presents three proofs that God cannot be in a direction. First, Sanusi argues that occupying a direction entails being a body (jism), and God cannot be a body. Second, if God were in a direction, He would either be larger or smaller than that direction, requiring a determinant (mukhassis) to specify one size, which implies origination. Third, if in a direction, God would be subject to motion or rest, both of which are originated (hadith); thus what cannot be free of them is originated. The conclusion is that direction (jiha) is impossible for God.

Key Terms
جهة (jiha)
مخصص (mukhassis)
حدوث (huduth)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that God could be in a direction without needing a cause because He is eternal.
Correction: The argument shows that any specific direction would require a cause for that specification, which contradicts God's self-sufficiency.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi's third argument, what does being in a direction necessitate?
A) Being a body
B) Needing a determinant
C) Being eternal
D) Having limits

Key Takeaway
God cannot be in a direction because that would require a determinant, implying origination, which is impossible for God.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If God is not confined to any direction, then He is equally present everywhere. Do you live as though God is closer to you than your own jugular vein, or do you subtly imagine Him far away? What daily habit could you adopt to remind yourself of His immediate presence?
?
This proof shows that God is utterly independent, needing no specifier or cause. Are there areas of your life where you act as though God needs your worship, your charity, or your obedience to be complete? How might acknowledging His absolute independence transform your relationship with Him?
?
The proof challenges the notion that God is 'above' in a spatial sense. When you pray, do you unconsciously direct your heart towards a physical place or direction? How can you train yourself to turn solely to the One who is beyond all directions?

The Salaf's Refraining from Ta'wil: Not Literalism, but Caution
Sanusi explains why some Salaf refrained from interpreting apparent verses.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Salaf refrained from interpreting certain Qur'anic verses—not because they accepted literal anthropomorphic meanings, but because they recognized multiple valid interpretations without knowing which was intended.

Core Idea
The Salaf's refraining from ta'wil was caution, not literalism.

A common misunderstanding about the early Muslims (Salaf) is that they believed in the literal, anthropomorphic meanings of verses like 'istawa' (He established Himself). However, Sanusi clarifies that their restraint (tawaqquf) was a sign of scholarly caution, not a belief in impossibility. In this passage, he explains the real reason behind their approach and defends their honor.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the literal translation. Let the author's own words set the context.
Notice the strong language: 'Far be it from them!' and 'How ugly it is to think evil.'
2
Identify the misconception and correction
Sanusi identifies a wrong belief that some had about the Salaf. Find what that wrong belief is and what the actual truth is.
The misconception is that the Salaf believed literal meanings; the correction is that they refrained due to multiple valid interpretations.
3
Reflect on the lesson's application
Think about how this passage teaches us to avoid hasty judgments about earlier scholars. Consider the principle that tawaqquf is a valid method.
This connects to the broader value of scholarly caution.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وسببُ وَهْمِ مَنْ نقلَ ذلكَ عن بعض السلف : ما عُرِفَ منهم رضيَ اللهُ تعالى عنهم مِنَ التوقُفِ عن تأويل الظواهر المستحيلة ; نحو عَلَى الْعَرْشِ اسْتَوَى ﴾ [طه : ٥] وما أشبهَهُ ، فتُوهَّمَ أَنَّ وقفَهم عن تأويلها لاعتقادهم ظواهرها ! وحاشاهم مِنْ ذلك ، وإنَّما وقفوا عن تعيين تأويل لها ; لتعدُّدِ التأويلات الصحيحةِ مِنْ غيرِ علم بالمراد منها ، بعد قطعهم بأنَّ الظواهر المستحيلة غيرُ مرادةٍ ألبتةَ ، وما أقبحَ أن يُظَنَّ السوءُ بِمَنْ لا يليقُ بهِ !
And the reason for the misconception of those who transmitted that about some of the Salaf: what was known of them - may Allah be pleased with them - of refraining (tawaqquf) from interpretation (ta'wil) of impossible apparent meanings, such as {He established Himself over the Throne} and what resembles it, so it was mistakenly thought that their refraining from interpreting them was due to their belief in their apparent meanings! Far be it from them! Rather, they refrained from specifying an interpretation for them due to the multiplicity of correct interpretations without knowledge of the intended meaning from among them, after their certainty that the impossible apparent meanings are absolutely not intended. And how ugly it is to think evil of those to whom it is not befitting!
Source pages p. 247

Commentary
This passage explains a common misunderstanding about the Salaf. The author identifies the root cause: the Salaf were known to refrain (tawaqquf) from assigning specific interpretations to certain verses whose apparent meanings are impossible for Allah, like 'istawa' on the Throne. Some wrongly assumed that this refraining meant they believed the literal, anthropomorphic meanings. The author exclaims 'far be it from them!' and clarifies: they refrained from specifying an interpretation because there are multiple valid interpretations and they did not have definitive knowledge of which was intended. However, they were absolutely certain that the impossible apparent meanings were not intended at all. The author concludes by condemning the ugliness of thinking ill of such people. The nuance: tawaqquf is a sign of caution, not literalism.

Key Terms
توقُف
تأويل
ظواهر مستحيلة
مراد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some people thought that the Salaf believed in the literal anthropomorphic meanings of verses like 'istawa'.
Correction: Sanusi clarifies that the Salaf refrained from interpretation because multiple valid interpretations existed and they lacked knowledge of the intended one, while being certain that the literal meaning was not intended.

Checkpoint
Why did some Salaf refrain from interpreting verses like 'istawa'?
A) They believed the literal meaning
B) They were unsure of which correct interpretation was intended
C) They denied the verses
D) They had no knowledge of Arabic

Key Takeaway
The Salaf's tawaqquf was an act of caution and reverence, not a rejection of metaphorical interpretation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Sanusi says 'how ugly it is to think evil of those to whom it is not befitting.' Have you ever assumed the worst about a scholar or a group of Muslims in theological matters? Will you repent from that suspicion and give the benefit of the doubt as the Salaf deserve?
?
The Salaf held back from specifying a ta'wil out of caution and reverence for Allah. In your own life, where are you tempted to speak about Allah's attributes without knowledge? Are you willing to remain silent when you lack certainty, just as they did?
?
Do you have the humility to admit that there may be multiple correct interpretations of a verse, and that you might not know which is intended? What would it cost your ego to accept that and refrain from speculating?

Denying Direction Does Not Deny Existence
Sanusi refutes a false inference about divine transcendence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that denying direction for Allah does not entail denying His existence, because existence is not limited to spatial categories like bodies.

Core Idea
Transcendence does not equal non-existence.

Sanusi addresses a common misunderstanding: when we affirm that Allah has no direction, some may mistakenly think we are denying His existence. He explains that this error arises only if one assumes existence is confined to bodies. Since Allah is beyond bodily attributes, negating direction is consistent with affirming His existence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the literal translation. Notice the tone: Sanusi calls the statement 'clear speech' and warns against misconception.
The passage ends mid-sentence; the incomplete clause 'this is a misconception of one who confined' implies confined existence to bodies.
2
Identify the list of negations
Sanusi lists attributes denied from Allah: not a part, not subsisting in a body, not described by size, not in a direction, not having a direction. This list clarifies what denying direction does and does not entail.
3
Understand the false inference
Someone might think: 'If Allah has no direction, then He does not exist.' Sanusi identifies this as a misconception of one who limits existence to bodies.
The false inference relies on an implicit premise: only bodies exist.
4
Reflect on the refutation
Since Allah is not a body, the properties of bodies (like direction) do not apply. Negating a property that does not apply does not negate existence.
This shows that divine transcendence does not imply non-existence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

And his statement: 'And that He also has no direction...' to its end: clear speech that does not need explanation, and one should not imagine concerning the Supreme Essence - since it is not a part (juz') nor subsisting in a body (jirm), nor described by smallness or bigness, and it is not in a direction nor does it have a direction - that that is a negation of its existence; because this is a misconception of one who confined
Source pages p. 247

Commentary
This passage refutes a false inference. The author comments on a previous statement asserting that Allah has no direction. He says it is self-evident and needs no explanation. Then he warns: do not imagine that denying direction for the Supreme Essence - which is not a part, not subsisting in a body, not described by size, not in a direction, and not having a direction - is a denial of His existence. That would be the misconception of someone who confines existence to bodies. In other words, existence is not limited to spatial entities. The passage ends with 'this is a misconception of one who confined...' suggesting a continuation explaining what such a person confined existence to. The core point: transcendence does not equal non-existence.

Misconception: Denying direction for Allah is equivalent to denying His existence.
Correction: Existence is not limited to bodies; Allah transcends spatial properties, so negating direction does not negate existence.

Negation of direction does not entail negation of existence, because existence is not confined to bodies.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
If you truly believed that Allah has no direction and is not a body, how would that change your attitude in salah or dua? Would you feel more intimate or more awe? Commit to one practical change that reflects this truth.

The False Analogy: Limiting God to a Body
Sanusi refutes the first erroneous group that declares God is a body.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why some mistakenly affirm that God is a body due to a false analogy, and how this error arises from confining existence to physical objects.

Core Idea
Denying physical attributes to God is not denial of His existence—it's a failure of imagination.

Sanusi exposes a critical error: some people, unable to conceive of existence beyond bodies and accidents, fall into the trap of affirming that God must be a body, albeit a unique one. This lesson unpacks that dangerous analogy and its root cause.

Guided Path
1
Understand the false illusion
Recognize that the false illusion (al-wahm al-kadhib) limits all existence to bodies and their properties. Without this assumption, the error would not occur.
This illusion is the foundation of both groups' mistakes.
2
See how it leads to affirming a bodily God
Notice how some, unable to deny God's existence, conclude that He must be a body—though unlike other bodies—to fit their limited worldview.
They misinterpret the verse 'There is nothing like Him' to support this.
3
Analyze the misinterpretation of the Quran
Examine the distorted reading of Quran 42:11, where 'like' is taken to mean resemblance among bodies, ignoring His transcendence.
This shows how preconceived notions can corrupt scriptural understanding.
4
Recognize the root cause: false analogy
Identify that the error stems from comparing what is unseen (God) to what is seen (bodies) without a common ground—a flawed qiyas.
Sanusi explicitly states this as the cause of perdition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقوله : ( وألا تكون له هو أيضاً جهة ... ) إلى آخره : كلام ظاهر لا يحتاج إلى شرحٍ ، ولا يُتَوَهَّمُ في الذات العليَّةِ - إذْ لم تكن جزماً ولا قائمة بالجِرْمِ ، ولا تتَّصفُ بصغرٍ ولا كِبَرِ ، وليسَتْ في جهةٍ ولا لها جهةٌ - أنَّ ذلك نفي لوجودِها (۱) ؛ لأنَّ هذا توهُمُ مَنْ حصرَ الموجودات فيما تخيَّلَ مِنَ الأجرامِ والقائم بها ، ولذلك تجد صاحبَ هذا الوهم الكاذب لحصرِهِ الموجوداتِ في الأجرام والقائم بها ، وادعائه استحالة موجود غيرهما .. تارةً يوافق العقل على وجوبِ افتقار الحوادثِ إلى مُحدِثِ ، لكنَّهُ يعارض الوهم الكاذب عندما يريدُ أن يثبت وجوبَ مخالفتِهِ تعالى لجميع الحوادثِ : فمنهم من لم يصحبه التوفيق في دفع ما عارضهُ مِنْ هذا الوهم الكاذب، فجزمَ - والعياذ بالله تعالى - بأنَّ مُوجِدَ العالم جِرْم مِنَ الأجرام ، وإن لم يماثله شيء منها في الحُسْنِ والجمال ، وهو معنى قوله تعالى : ﴿ لَيْسَ كَمِثْلِهِ شَيْ﴾ [الشورى : ١١] عند هذا المطرودِ المسخوط عليه . تعالى الله عن ذلك ، وسبب ضلالِهِ : أَنَّهُ قاسَ ما لم يَرَ على ما رأى بغير جامع ، فهلك والعياذ بالله تعالى ، ولا حول ولا قوة إلا بالله . ومن هؤلاء مَنْ تبيَّنَ لَهُ أنَّ مُوجِدَ العالم لو كانَ جِرْماً لوجبَ حدوثه ، ولزم في ذلكَ الدَّورُ أو التسلسلُ ، فجزم لأجل هذا معَ ما رسخ في قلبِهِ مِنَ الوهم الكاذب - وهو أنَّ كلَّ موجود لا بد وأن يكون جِرْماً أو قائماً بهِ ـ أنَّ العالم حدث لنفسِهِ بغيرِ مُحدِثِ ! وجاءَتِ المصيبةُ للفريقين ؛ مِنْ حِرْمانِ التوفيق والتأييد وعدم إمدادِ اللهِ تعالى العقل بالنظرِ والفكر السديد ، فأصغى بأُذنِهِ لكاذب الوهم والخيالِ ، الخائضِ فيما ليس أهلاً لهُ مِنْ أحكام ذي
And his statement: 'And that He also has no direction...' to its end: is clear speech needing no explanation. And it should not be imagined concerning the Supreme Essence - since it is not a body nor subsisting in a body, nor is it described with smallness or bigness, nor is it in a direction nor does it have a direction - that this is a negation of its existence; because this is the illusion of one who limits existents to what he imagines from bodies and what subsists in them. Therefore you find the possessor of this false illusion, due to his limiting of existents to bodies and what subsists in them and his claim of the impossibility of an existent other than them, sometimes agrees with reason upon the necessity of the need of contingent things for a Maker, but he opposes the false illusion when he wants to establish the necessity of His transcendence above all contingent things. Among them is one whom success does not accompany in repelling what opposes him from this false illusion, so he firmly decided - and refuge is sought with Allah - that the Maker of the world is a body from among bodies, even if nothing from them resembles Him in beauty and perfection. And that is the meaning of His statement: 'There is nothing like Him' [Shura 11] according to this rejected, wrathful one. Exalted is Allah above that. And the cause of his misguidance is that he analogized what he did not see to what he saw without a common ground, so he perished, refuge is sought with Allah, and there is no power nor strength except with Allah. And among them is one for whom it became clear that if the Maker of the world were a body, its temporality would be necessary, and there would result from that an infinite regress or circularity. So due to this, with what was fixed in his heart from the false illusion - that every existent must be a body or subsisting in one - he firmly decided that the world came to be by itself without a Maker. And the calamity came upon both groups: from the deprivation of success and support and the lack of Allah's supplying the intellect with sound reflection and thought. So he listens with his ear to the false illusion and imagination, plunging into matters he is not qualified for from the judgments of the Possessor of...
Source pages p. 247

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of those who, due to a false imagination that all existence is limited to bodies and their accidents (properties), mistakenly think that denying physical attributes to Allah (like direction, body) is a denial of His existence. The author explains that this error arises from confining existence to what the imagination can conceive. The author then details two disastrous outcomes that result from this false premise: (1) Some, unable to reconcile God's transcendence with their limited view, end up affirming that God is a body (though unlike other bodies), misinterpreting verses like 'There is nothing like Him' to mean He is a body but unique. Their error is drawing an analogy without a common ground. (2) Others, realizing that if God were a body He would be temporal and that would lead to infinite regress or circularity, but still holding the false premise that every existent must be a body or accident, conclude that the world came to be by itself without a Creator. Both groups are misguided because they follow a false imagination instead of sound reason and revelation. The passage ends by lamenting that these people listen only to their fantasy and delve into matters beyond their capacity.

Key Terms
الوهم الكاذب
الأجرام
القائم بها

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Denying physical attributes to God (like body, direction) is equivalent to denying His existence.
Correction: Denying physical attributes is necessary for divine transcendence; existence is not limited to bodies.

Checkpoint

A) Rejection of causality
B) False analogy without common ground
C) Misunderstanding of the verse 'There is nothing like Him'
D) Denial of the need for a Creator

Key Takeaway
The false analogy of comparing God to physical objects leads some to affirm a bodily Creator, which is a grave error.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever caught yourself imagining Allah in a way that resembles created things, even subtly? What would it take for you to sincerely affirm His transcendence without any mental image? Resolve to deliberately banish every human-like image when you say 'Allahu Akbar' this week.
?
The misguided person analogized the unseen to the seen without a common ground. In what areas of your life do you tend to judge Allah's actions based on human standards of fairness or justice? How can you train yourself to submit to His absolute transcendence?
?
The verse 'There is nothing like Him' was twisted by some to mean He is a unique body. How might you be guilty of twisting divine attributes to fit your own limited understanding? Commit to studying the names and attributes with tanzih as your foundation.

The Deadly Conclusion: Denying the Creator
Sanusi exposes the second group that denies the Creator due to false premises.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the false premise that all existents are bodies leads some to atheism, because they realize a physical God would imply infinite regress yet cannot conceive of a non-physical Creator.

Core Idea
A false premise, even with correct reasoning, can lead to disastrous atheism.

Sanusi reveals an even more tragic outcome of the false imagination: some, seeing that a bodily Creator leads to logical absurdity (infinite regress or circularity), reject the Creator altogether rather than abandon their limiting assumption. This lesson exposes the error of those who deny existence of a Creator based on a flawed premise.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the second group's reasoning
Understand that these individuals correctly see that if the Creator were a body, He would be temporal, leading to infinite regress or circularity.
They have logical consistency but a false starting point.
2
Identify the false premise they cling to
They maintain the false illusion that every existent must be a body or accident, so they cannot accept a non-physical Creator.
This premise prevents them from reaching the truth.
3
See their disastrous conclusion
Because they cannot conceive of a non-physical Creator and cannot accept a bodily Creator, they conclude the world came to be by itself without a Maker.
This is the ultimate logical consequence of their false premise.
4
Reflect on the lamentation
Sanusi laments that both groups are deprived of divine support and follow a false imagination, plunging into matters beyond their capacity.
The lesson warns against relying on flawed assumptions.

وقوله : ( وألا تكون له هو أيضاً جهة ... ) إلى آخره : كلام ظاهر لا يحتاج إلى شرحٍ ، ولا يُتَوَهَّمُ في الذات العليَّةِ - إذْ لم تكن جزماً ولا قائمة بالجِرْمِ ، ولا تتَّصفُ بصغرٍ ولا كِبَرِ ، وليسَتْ في جهةٍ ولا لها جهةٌ - أنَّ ذلك نفي لوجودِها (۱) ؛ لأنَّ هذا توهُمُ مَنْ حصرَ الموجودات فيما تخيَّلَ مِنَ الأجرامِ والقائم بها ، ولذلك تجد صاحبَ هذا الوهم الكاذب لحصرِهِ الموجوداتِ في الأجرام والقائم بها ، وادعائه استحالة موجود غيرهما .. تارةً يوافق العقل على وجوبِ افتقار الحوادثِ إلى مُحدِثِ ، لكنَّهُ يعارض الوهم الكاذب عندما يريدُ أن يثبت وجوبَ مخالفتِهِ تعالى لجميع الحوادثِ : فمنهم من لم يصحبه التوفيق في دفع ما عارضهُ مِنْ هذا الوهم الكاذب، فجزمَ - والعياذ بالله تعالى - بأنَّ مُوجِدَ العالم جِرْم مِنَ الأجرام ، وإن لم يماثله شيء منها في الحُسْنِ والجمال ، وهو معنى قوله تعالى : ﴿ لَيْسَ كَمِثْلِهِ شَيْ﴾ [الشورى : ١١] عند هذا المطرودِ المسخوط عليه . تعالى الله عن ذلك ، وسبب ضلالِهِ : أَنَّهُ قاسَ ما لم يَرَ على ما رأى بغير جامع ، فهلك والعياذ بالله تعالى ، ولا حول ولا قوة إلا بالله . ومن هؤلاء مَنْ تبيَّنَ لَهُ أنَّ مُوجِدَ العالم لو كانَ جِرْماً لوجبَ حدوثه ، ولزم في ذلكَ الدَّورُ أو التسلسلُ ، فجزم لأجل هذا معَ ما رسخ في قلبِهِ مِنَ الوهم الكاذب - وهو أنَّ كلَّ موجود لا بد وأن يكون جِرْماً أو قائماً بهِ ـ أنَّ العالم حدث لنفسِهِ بغيرِ مُحدِثِ ! وجاءَتِ المصيبةُ للفريقين ؛ مِنْ حِرْمانِ التوفيق والتأييد وعدم إمدادِ اللهِ تعالى العقل بالنظرِ والفكر السديد ، فأصغى بأُذنِهِ لكاذب الوهم والخيالِ ، الخائضِ فيما ليس أهلاً لهُ مِنْ أحكام ذي
And his statement: 'And that He also has no direction...' to its end: is clear speech needing no explanation. And it should not be imagined concerning the Supreme Essence - since it is not a body nor subsisting in a body, nor is it described with smallness or bigness, nor is it in a direction nor does it have a direction - that this is a negation of its existence; because this is the illusion of one who limits existents to what he imagines from bodies and what subsists in them. Therefore you find the possessor of this false illusion, due to his limiting of existents to bodies and what subsists in them and his claim of the impossibility of an existent other than them, sometimes agrees with reason upon the necessity of the need of contingent things for a Maker, but he opposes the false illusion when he wants to establish the necessity of His transcendence above all contingent things. Among them is one whom success does not accompany in repelling what opposes him from this false illusion, so he firmly decided - and refuge is sought with Allah - that the Maker of the world is a body from among bodies, even if nothing from them resembles Him in beauty and perfection. And that is the meaning of His statement: 'There is nothing like Him' [Shura 11] according to this rejected, wrathful one. Exalted is Allah above that. And the cause of his misguidance is that he analogized what he did not see to what he saw without a common ground, so he perished, refuge is sought with Allah, and there is no power nor strength except with Allah. And among them is one for whom it became clear that if the Maker of the world were a body, its temporality would be necessary, and there would result from that an infinite regress or circularity. So due to this, with what was fixed in his heart from the false illusion - that every existent must be a body or subsisting in one - he firmly decided that the world came to be by itself without a Maker. And the calamity came upon both groups: from the deprivation of success and support and the lack of Allah's supplying the intellect with sound reflection and thought. So he listens with his ear to the false illusion and imagination, plunging into matters he is not qualified for from the judgments of the Possessor of...
Source pages p. 247

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of those who, due to a false imagination that all existence is limited to bodies and their accidents (properties), mistakenly think that denying physical attributes to Allah (like direction, body) is a denial of His existence. The author explains that this error arises from confining existence to what the imagination can conceive. The author then details two disastrous outcomes that result from this false premise: (1) Some, unable to reconcile God's transcendence with their limited view, end up affirming that God is a body (though unlike other bodies), misinterpreting verses like 'There is nothing like Him' to mean He is a body but unique. Their error is drawing an analogy without a common ground. (2) Others, realizing that if God were a body He would be temporal and that would lead to infinite regress or circularity, but still holding the false premise that every existent must be a body or accident, conclude that the world came to be by itself without a Creator. Both groups are misguided because they follow a false imagination instead of sound reason and revelation. The passage ends by lamenting that these people listen only to their fantasy and delve into matters beyond their capacity.

Key Terms
الدور
التسلسل
الوهم الكاذب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That existence must be limited to bodies and accidents, so if a bodily Creator is impossible, there is no Creator at all.
Correction: The Creator is not a body; He is beyond physical categories, and denying a bodily Creator does not negate His existence.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why do some people conclude that the world came to be by itself without a Creator?
A) They believe in atheism from the start.
B) They realize a bodily Creator leads to infinite regress, and they cannot accept a non-physical Creator due to their false illusion.
C) They deny causality altogether.
D) They follow a different religion.

Key Takeaway
Clinging to a false premise, even with good logic, can lead to outright denial of God—a disaster of the intellect.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
What false premises about Allah or existence might you be unconsciously holding that, if followed logically, could weaken your iman? Are you willing to examine them in light of revelation, even if it feels uncomfortable?
?
Sanusi says the misguided ones were deprived of divine success because they relied on false imagination. Is there an area in your life where you trust your own reasoning more than the guidance of the Quran and Sunnah? What change will you make today to submit your intellect to Allah?
?
The calamity of the two groups came from assuming that truth must fit their limited framework. In what ways are you limiting Allah by your own assumptions? Commit to one specific step this week to study Allah's names and attributes without imposing human categories.

Divine Transcendence
beginner

Refuting the False Imagination: Lack of Perception Does Not Imply Non-Existence
Sanusi refutes the false imagination with the principle that lack of perception does not imply non-existence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sanusi refutes the false imagination that inability to perceive Allah implies His non-existence, using the principle that lack of perception does not entail non-existence.

Core Idea
Not perceiving a thing does not mean it does not exist; perception requires divine opening.

Sanusi begins by diagnosing the disaster that befalls those who rely on false imagination: they are deprived of divine success and sound thought. He then exposes the error of assuming that if we cannot perceive an essence that is neither body nor accident, it must not exist. This lesson focuses on his refutation of that fallacy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two groups
Read the opening lines and note which two groups Sanusi refers to as suffering disaster due to false imagination.
2
Understand the core argument
Sanusi states that the false imagination only produces a lack of perception, and that lack of perception does not logically imply non-existence. Grasp this key principle.
3
Reflect on the analogies
Consider the examples: knowing bodies and accidents, self-perception, and the inability of inanimate objects and animals to perceive things clear to others. How do these support the argument?
These analogies show that perception is dependent on divine opening.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وجاءت المصيبةُ للفريقين ؛ مِنْ حِرْمانِ التوفيق والتأييد وعدم إمدادِ اللهِ تعالى العقل بالنظرِ والفكر السديد ، فأصغى بأُذنِهِ لكاذب الوهم والخيالِ ، الخائضِ فيما ليس أهلاً لهُ مِنْ أحكام ذي الجلال ، الذي لا يحصرُهُ حدّ ولا يُتَعَرَّفُ بمثالٍ ، ولم يعلم هذا المصغي أذنَهُ للوهم أنَّهُ ليسَ معَ هذا الوهم إلا عدم الشعور بذاتِ ليسَتْ بِجِرْمٍ ولا عَرَضٍ ، ولا يلزمُ مِنْ عدم الشعور بشيء عدم وجودِهِ ألم يعلم العاقلُ : بأنَّ ما اطَّلَعَ عليهِ مِنَ الأجرام والقائم بها ؛ لولا أنَّ الله تعالى فتح لهُ مِنَ العلم بهِ . لَمّا أدرك منه شيئاً ؟! بل لو لم يفتح لهُ في الشعورِ بذاتِهِ لَمَا شعرَ بها أصلاً ، ولينظر إلى الجمادات وإلى الحيوانات المماثلة له كيف تعذَّرَ عليها إدراك ما لم يفتح لها في إدراكه وإن كان واضحاً عند غيرها . فالذات العلية وجودها مُحقَّق واجبٌ ، أظهرُ مِنْ كُلِّ ظاهرٍ ، وكلُّ جزء مِنْ أجزاء العالم وكلُّ صفةٍ مِنْ صفاتِهِ تلهج بذلك بلسان الحال وتُفصِحُ بهِ أبينَ وأوضحَ مِنْ إفصاح المقال ، لكن مع ذلكَ لا طريق إلى معرفة حقيقتها بما فتح لنا تعالى في إدراكه مِنْ حقائقِ الكائناتِ الحادثة ؛ إذ لا مثلَ لهُ تعالى منها جلَّ وعزَّ ، ولم يخلق تعالى لنا عِلْماً بحقيقةِ ذاتِهِ الواجبةِ الوجودِ ، كما لم يخلق تعالى للجماداتِ وكثيرٍ مِنَ الحيوانات إدراكاً بما هو مُحقَّقُ الوجودِ مِنْ أنفسها القريبة إليها جداً فما فوق ذلك ، ولا علم لأحدٍ مِنَ الكائناتِ إِلا بما علَّمَهُ لهُ مولاه جلَّ وعزَّ ، وفتح له فيه بفضلِهِ وقد فتح سبحانَهُ بفضلِهِ في معرفتِنا بوجودِهِ وصفاتِهِ على وجه تميَّزَ
And the disaster came to both groups: from deprivation of divine success and support, and the lack of Allah the Exalted supplying the intellect with sound contemplation and thought. So he lent his ear to the false imagination and fancy, which meddles in matters of which it is not worthy concerning the judgments of the Possessor of Majesty, whom no limit encompasses nor is known by an example. And this one who lent his ear to the false imagination did not know that with this false imagination there is only the lack of perception of an essence that is neither a body nor an accident. And from the lack of perception of something, its non-existence does not necessarily follow. Does the rational person not know that what he has come to know of bodies and what subsists in them – were it not that Allah the Exalted opened for him knowledge of it, he would not have perceived anything of it? Rather, if He had not opened for him perception of his own self, he would not have perceived it at all. And let him look at inanimate objects and the animals similar to him – how they are prevented from perceiving what He has not opened for them to perceive, even if it is clear to others. So the Supreme Essence – its existence is certain and necessary, more manifest than every manifest thing. Every part of the world and every attribute of it proclaims that by the tongue of state and makes it clearer and more obvious than the clarity of speech. But despite that, there is no way to know its reality through what the Exalted has opened for us to perceive of the realities of contingent beings, for there is no likeness to Him, the Mighty and Majestic, among them. And the Exalted has not created for us knowledge of the reality of His essence, the Necessary of existence, just as He has not created for inanimate objects and many animals perception of what is certainly existent of their own selves, which are very close to them, and so on beyond that. And there is no knowledge for any of the beings except what his Lord, the Mighty and Majestic, has taught him and opened for him through His grace. And He, glorified, has opened through His grace for our knowledge of His existence and attributes in a manner that distinguishes...
Source pages p. 248

Commentary
This passage begins by stating that both groups (the anthropomorphists and the atheists) suffer the disaster of being deprived of divine success. Sanusi then explains that the false imagination leads one to listen to fancy and meddle in matters beyond its capacity, namely, the judgments concerning the Possessor of Majesty. The key refutation is that the false imagination only gives a 'lack of perception' (ʿadam al-shuʿūr) of an essence that is neither a body nor an accident. But lack of perception does not entail non-existence. Sanusi uses an analogy: humans only know bodies and accidents because Allah opened knowledge to them; without that opening, they would not perceive them. Similarly, if Allah had not opened perception of one's own self, one would not perceive it. He points to inanimate objects and animals that cannot perceive many things that are clear to others. Therefore, inability to perceive Allah's essence does not mean He does not exist. On the contrary, Allah's existence is the most manifest, as every part of the world proclaims it by the 'tongue of state' (lisān al-ḥāl). However, despite this manifest existence, there is no way to know His true reality (ḥaqīqat dhātihi) through the realities of contingent beings, because there is no likeness to Him. Allah has not created for us knowledge of His essence, just as He has not created perception for inanimate objects and many animals of their own existences, which are very close to them. The passage concludes that all knowledge comes only from Allah's teaching and grace, and He has opened for us knowledge of His existence and attributes in a way that distinguishes (perhaps meaning distinguishes us from other creatures). The text ends abruptly, but the argument is complete: Allah's existence is known through His signs, but His essence is unknowable.

Key Terms
عدم الشعور
ذات ليست بجرم ولا عرض

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If we cannot perceive something with our senses or intellect, it must not exist.
Correction: Sanusi shows that lack of perception does not entail non-existence; many things exist that we do not perceive, and perception itself depends on divine opening.

Checkpoint
What is the key principle Sanusi uses to refute the false imagination?
A) The false imagination is always wrong.
B) Lack of perception does not imply non-existence.
C) Only the intellect can know Allah.
D) Perception is the only proof of existence.

Key Takeaway
Lack of perception of Allah does not mean He does not exist; perception is dependent on divine opening.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do I sometimes measure God's reality by my own feelings of His presence, forgetting that my perception is a gift He may give or withhold? How can I train myself to trust His existence even when I do not 'feel' Him?
?
When I experience doubt about matters of faith, do I immediately assume that what I cannot grasp intellectually must be false? What would change if I humbly acknowledged my dependence on Allah for every bit of knowledge?
?
If even my own self-awareness is a direct gift from Allah, how should that reshape my understanding of my own existence? Does my life reflect gratitude for this constant, unearned gift of consciousness?

Divine Transcendence
beginner

The Manifest Existence and Unknowable Essence of Allah
Sanusi affirms Allah's manifest existence and explains the unknowability of His essence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Allah's existence is the most manifest reality, yet His essence is beyond human comprehension and cannot be known through contingent beings.

Core Idea
Allah's existence is absolutely manifest, but His essence is utterly transcendent and unknowable.

Having refuted the false imagination, Sanusi now turns to the positive affirmation of Allah's existence and transcendence. He declares that the Supreme Essence has necessary and certain existence, more manifest than anything else, and that every part of the world proclaims this. Yet, he cautions, we cannot know Allah's true reality because He has no likeness and has not created for us the capacity to comprehend His essence. This lesson explores this dual truth: manifest existence, hidden essence.

Guided Path
1
Read the affirmative declaration
Notice how Sanusi shifts from refutation to positive statement: 'So the Supreme Essence – its existence is certain and necessary, more manifest than every manifest thing.'
2
Understand the witness of the world
Sanusi says that every part of the world proclaims Allah's existence by the 'tongue of state' (lisān al-ḥāl). Reflect on what this means: the very existence of contingent things points to the Necessary Being.
3
Grasp the limitation on knowledge
Despite manifest existence, there is no way to know Allah's essence through contingent realities. Sanusi gives two reasons: no likeness to Him, and Allah has not created for us the capacity to know His essence.
This is a crucial point: knowledge of existence does not imply knowledge of essence.
4
Consider the comparison with animals
Sanusi compares our inability to know Allah's essence to inanimate objects and animals that lack perception of even their own selves. This illustrates that lack of knowledge is not due to non-existence but due to limited capacity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Because we cannot know Allah's essence, we cannot know Him at all.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, why can we not know Allah's true essence?
A) Because Allah's existence is not manifest.
B) Because there is no likeness to Him in contingent beings and He has not created for us the capacity to know it.

D) Because only prophets can know His essence.

Key Takeaway
Allah's existence is the most manifest reality, but His essence is beyond human knowledge; we know Him only through His existence and attributes as He has taught us.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If Allah's existence is more manifest than everything, why do you often live as if He is absent? What would change today if you truly allowed yourself to feel His manifest existence in every breath you take?
?
You know you cannot know Allah's essence, yet you still try to imagine Him. What does this passage reveal about the folly of that? How can you train your heart to be content with knowing His existence and attributes, surrendering the rest to His majesty?
?
The passage says Allah has not created knowledge of His essence for you, just as He has not for inanimate objects. How does that humble your intellect? What practical step will you take this week to stop trying to 'figure out' Allah and instead worship Him on His own terms?

Divine Transcendence
beginner
4 min
Refuting the Misconception of Non-Perception
Sanusi refutes the claim that lack of perception implies non-existence using the analogy of animals and the gift of perception.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that lack of sensory or intellectual perception does not imply non-existence, and that perception is a gift from God.

Core Idea
Not perceiving something doesn't mean it doesn't exist.

Sanusi begins by addressing a common mistake: assuming that what we cannot perceive does not exist. He shows that perception itself depends on God's will, using the example of our own inability to perceive our own selves without divine opening. This lesson explores that argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation. Notice how Sanusi sets up the objection from imagination (wahm).
The passage uses a rhetorical question to engage the reader.
2
Identify the objection from imagination
The objection is that if we don't perceive something (like God's essence), it must not exist. Sanusi points out that imagination alone cannot determine existence.
The word 'wahm' refers to the estimative faculty, which can be mistaken.
3
See the refutation with examples
Sanusi asks: do we perceive our own selves without God's opening? No. And animals cannot perceive many things that are obvious to us. Therefore, non-perception does not prove non-existence.
The analogy with animals is powerful to show that lack of perception is common.
4
Understand the theological principle
The key is that existence is independent of our perception. God exists even if we do not perceive Him directly.
This prepares for the next lesson on God's manifest existence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الجلال ، الذي لا يحصرُهُ حدّ ولا يُتَعَرَّفُ بمثالٍ ، ولم يعلم هذا المصغي أذنَهُ للوهم أنَّهُ ليسَ معَ هذا الوهم إلا عدم الشعور بذاتِ ليسَتْ بِجِرْمٍ ولا عَرَضٍ ، ولا يلزمُ مِنْ عدم الشعور بشيء عدم وجودِهِ ألم يعلم العاقلُ : بأنَّ ما اطَّلَعَ عليهِ مِنَ الأجرام والقائم بها ؛ لولا أنَّ الله تعالى فتح لهُ مِنَ العلم بهِ . لَمّا أدرك منه شيئاً ؟! بل لو لم يفتح لهُ في الشعورِ بذاتِهِ لَمَا شعرَ بها أصلاً ، ولينظر إلى الجمادات وإلى الحيوانات المماثلة له كيف تعذَّرَ عليها إدراك ما لم يفتح لها في إدراكه وإن كان واضحاً عند غيرها . جلال الذاتِ العليَّة في ظهورها وبطونها ] فالذات العلية وجودها مُحقَّق واجبٌ ، أظهرُ مِنْ كُلِّ ظاهرٍ ، وكلُّ جزء مِنْ أجزاء العالم وكلُّ صفةٍ مِنْ صفاتِهِ تلهج بذلك بلسان الحال وتُفصِحُ بهِ أبينَ وأوضحَ مِنْ إفصاح المقال ، لكن مع ذلكَ لا طريق إلى معرفة حقيقتها بما فتح لنا تعالى في إدراكه مِنْ حقائقِ الكائناتِ الحادثة ؛ إذ لا مثلَ لهُ تعالى منها جلَّ وعزَّ ، ولم يخلق تعالى لنا عِلْماً بحقيقةِ ذاتِهِ الواجبةِ الوجودِ ، كما لم يخلق تعالى للجماداتِ وكثيرٍ مِنَ الحيوانات إدراكاً بما هو مُحقَّقُ الوجودِ مِنْ أنفسها القريبة إليها جداً فما فوق ذلك ، ولا علم لأحدٍ مِنَ الكائناتِ إِلا بما علَّمَهُ لهُ مولاه جلَّ وعزَّ ، وفتح له فيه بفضلِهِ وقد فتح سبحانَهُ بفضلِهِ في معرفتِنا بوجودِهِ وصفاتِهِ على وجه تميَّزَ بهِ في عقولنا عن كل ما سواه ، وأعلمنا تعالى مِنَ البراهين ما عرفنا بهِ صدْقَ رُسُلِهِ على وجه عرفنا بهِ أحكامه المتوجهة إلينا ، وما وراء ذلكَ لا تتوقَّفُ عليهِ عبادة مولانا جل وعزَّ ولا إخلاص العبوديَّةِ لهُ تعالى ، ونحن عاجزون عن إدراكه إلا أن يتفضَّلَ سبحانه وتعالى بما يشاءُ مِنَ الإدراكِ بعد ، كما كنا عاجزينَ في أصل نشأتنا عن كل إدراك حتى تفضَّلَ سبحانَهُ بما شاءَ ، لهُ الحمدُ جلَّ وعلا كما يليقُ بهِ ، أَخْرَجَكُم مِّنْ بُطُونِ أُمَّهَيْكُمْ لَا تَعْلَمُونَ شَيْئًا) [النحل : ٧٨] . ومهما اعترضنا الوهم الغبيُّ الكاذبُ فيما عرفناه ضرورةً مِنَ العقائدِ بالبراهين القطعيَّة الصادقة .. قلنا له : اخسأ ، فلن تعدو قدرك (١) ، وليس هذا مقاماً يصلحُ لك حتى تُعلَّقَ بهِ سَرَّكَ ، فلا تتطاول إلى الحديثِ فيهِ ، وإنَّما هذا مقام لا يهتدي إليه إلا المعتنى بهِ ، الشريف الموفَّقُ مِنَ العقولِ ، وكم انقطع دونَ فِيحِ صحرائِهِ مِنَ الأَئِمَّةِ الفحول . لَعَمْرِي لَقَدْ طُفْتُ الْمَعَاهِدَ كُلَّهَا وَسَرَّحْتُ طَرْفِي بَيْنَ تِلْكَ الْمَعَالِمِ فَلَمْ أَرَ إِلا وَاضِعاً كَفَّ حَائِرٍ عَلَى ذَقَنِ أَوْ قَارِعاً سِنَّ نَادِمِ (٢)
The Majesty, which no limit confines nor is known by a likeness, and this one who lends his ear to imagination (al-wahm) does not know that with this imagination there is only lack of perception of an essence that is not a body nor an accident. And it does not follow from lack of perception of something its non-existence. Does not the rational person know that what he has observed of bodies and what subsists in them – if God had not opened for him knowledge of it, he would not have perceived anything of it? Indeed, if He had not opened for him perception of his own self, he would not have perceived it at all. And let him look at inanimate objects and animals similar to him how it was impossible for them to perceive what He did not open for them to perceive, even if it is clear to others. The majesty of the high essence in its manifestation and hiddenness. So the high essence: its existence is realized, necessary, more manifest than any manifest thing, and every part of the world and every attribute of it speaks of that in the tongue of state and makes it clear more clearly and plainly than the clarity of speech. But despite that, there is no way to know its reality through what He has opened to us in perceiving the realities of created beings; for there is no likeness to Him from them, exalted and mighty. And He did not create for us knowledge of the reality of His necessarily existent essence, just as He did not create for inanimate objects and many animals perception of what is realized in existence from their own selves that are very close to them, and beyond that. And there is no knowledge for any of the created beings except what his Master taught him and opened for him in it by His grace. And He has opened by His grace to our knowledge of His existence and attributes in a way that distinguishes Him in our minds from everything else. And He taught us from the proofs (al-barahin) what we know by it the truth of His messengers in a way that we know by it His laws directed to us. And what is beyond that, worship of our Master and sincerity of servitude to Him does not depend on it. And we are incapable of perceiving it unless He bestows as He wills from perception afterwards, just as we were incapable at the origin of our creation from all perception until He bestowed as He willed. To Him is praise, exalted and high, as befits Him. "He brought you out from the wombs of your mothers knowing nothing" [an-Nahl 16:78]. And whenever the stupid false imagination objects to us in what we know necessarily of beliefs by truthful definitive proofs, we say to it: "Begone, you will not exceed your capacity" (1), and this is not a place suitable for you to attach your secret to it. So do not stretch forward to speak in it. And this is a station that only the one who is cared for, the noble, the divinely guided intellects can find guidance to. And how many of the great imams have fallen short before the vastness of its desert. By my life, I have toured all the institutes and let my eye wander among those landmarks, and I saw only one placing a hand of astonishment on his chin or one gnashing the tooth of remorse. (2)
Source pages p. 249

Commentary
This passage is a multifaceted argument affirming the transcendence of God's essence and the epistemological limits of created beings. It begins by addressing a common objection from the estimative faculty (wahm): that if we do not perceive something, it does not exist. The author refutes this by noting that perception itself is a gift from God; we do not even perceive our own selves without His opening. He draws an analogy to inanimate objects and animals, which cannot perceive what is obvious to others, underscoring that lack of perception does not entail non-existence. 

Then follows a heading: 'The majesty of the high essence in its manifestation and hiddenness.' The author affirms that God's existence is necessary and more manifest than anything else; all of creation declares His existence in the 'tongue of state' more clearly than speech. Yet, despite this manifestness, we cannot know His reality (haqiqa) through created things because He has no likeness. 

The argument continues: God has not given us knowledge of the reality of His essence, just as He did not give animals knowledge of their own existence. All knowledge is solely by God's teaching and favor. What He has granted us is knowledge of His existence and attributes, enough to distinguish Him from all else, and proofs to verify the truth of His messengers and His revealed laws. Knowledge beyond this is not required for worship and sincerity of servitude. We are incapable of such perception unless God grants it, as He granted us perception from total ignorance at birth, as the Quranic verse states: 'He brought you out from the wombs of your mothers knowing nothing.'

Finally, the author dismisses any objection from a 'stupid false imagination' against the necessary beliefs known through definitive proofs. He quotes a hadith: 'Begone, you will not exceed your capacity,' and declares that this subject is too lofty for such objections; only divinely guided intellects can approach it. The passage concludes with two lines of poetry by al-Shahrastani, lamenting how many great scholars have fallen short before this vast topic.

Key Terms
الوهم
عدم الشعور
جلال الذات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That lack of sensory or intellectual perception of something implies its non-existence.
Correction: Perception is a gift from God; many things exist that we do not perceive, such as our own selves without divine opening.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, why does lack of perception not prove non-existence?
A) Because imagination is always false.
B) Because perception depends on God's opening; we don't even perceive ourselves without it.
C) Because God is a body and can be perceived.
D) Because only rational beings have perception.

Key Takeaway
Lack of perception does not imply non-existence; perception is a divine gift.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever doubted or denied something about your faith simply because you could not see or feel it? How does Sanusi's argument about animals perceiving only what God allows expose the weakness of that doubt? What will you do the next time such doubt arises?
?
The passage teaches that even your awareness of your own self is a gift from God. When have you taken your own consciousness for granted? How can you turn this realization into a moment of gratitude today?
?
Imagine you are the one 'lending your ear to imagination'—where in your life has your imagination led you to assume something false about Allah? What concrete step will you take to submit your imagination to the truth of this lesson?

Divine Transcendence
beginner

God's Manifest Existence and Hidden Essence
Sanusi sets forth the dual truth of God's manifest existence and hidden essence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that God's existence is the most manifest reality, yet His essence is unknowable, and that knowledge of His existence and attributes is sufficient for worship.

Core Idea
God's existence is obvious, but His essence is beyond our grasp.

After establishing that non-perception doesn't negate existence, Sanusi now affirms that God's existence is the most manifest thing. But he also clarifies that we cannot know God's essence—only His existence and attributes are taught to us. This lesson unpacks that balance.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the strong contrast between God's manifest existence and hidden essence.
The phrase 'لسان الحال' (tongue of state) is important: creation itself declares God's existence.
2
Identify the two key claims
First claim: God's existence is necessary and more manifest than anything. Second claim: Despite that, we cannot know His reality (haqiqa).
These two claims are not contradictory; they form a paradox of divine transcendence.
3
See the reason for unknowability
We cannot know God's essence because He has no likeness in creation, and God did not create that knowledge for us.
Sanusi compares this to animals not knowing their own existence.
4
Understand what God has taught us
God has taught us His existence and attributes sufficiently to distinguish Him from all else, and He has given proofs to verify His messengers and laws. This is enough for worship.
The keyword is 'كفاية' (sufficiency).

The Majesty, which no limit confines nor is known by a likeness, and this one who lends his ear to imagination (al-wahm) does not know that with this imagination there is only lack of perception of an essence that is not a body nor an accident. And it does not follow from lack of perception of something its non-existence. And let him look at inanimate objects and animals similar to him how it was impossible for them to perceive what He did not open for them to perceive, even if it is clear to others. The majesty of the high essence in its manifestation and hiddenness. So the high essence: its existence is realized, necessary, more manifest than any manifest thing, and every part of the world and every attribute of it speaks of that in the tongue of state and makes it clear more clearly and plainly than the clarity of speech. But despite that, there is no way to know its reality through what He has opened to us in perceiving the realities of created beings; for there is no likeness to Him from them, exalted and mighty. And He did not create for us knowledge of the reality of His necessarily existent essence, just as He did not create for inanimate objects and many animals perception of what is realized in existence from their own selves that are very close to them, and beyond that. And there is no knowledge for any of the created beings except what his Master taught him and opened for him in it by His grace. And He taught us from the proofs (al-barahin) what we know by it the truth of His messengers in a way that we know by it His laws directed to us. And what is beyond that, worship of our Master and sincerity of servitude to Him does not depend on it. And we are incapable of perceiving it unless He bestows as He wills from perception afterwards, just as we were incapable at the origin of our creation from all perception until He bestowed as He willed. And whenever the stupid false imagination objects to us in what we know necessarily of beliefs by truthful definitive proofs, we say to it: "Begone, you will not exceed your capacity" (1), and this is not a place suitable for you to attach your secret to it. What He has granted us is knowledge of His existence and attributes, enough to distinguish Him from all else, and proofs to verify the truth of His messengers and His revealed laws. Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That we must understand God's essence to worship Him properly or that His essence can be fully grasped.
Correction: Sanusi teaches that knowledge of God's existence and attributes is sufficient; knowledge of His essence is not given to us, nor is it required for worship.

Checkpoint
Why can we not know God's essence (haqiqa) according to Sanusi?
A) Because God's existence is not manifest enough.
B) Because He has no likeness in creation and God did not create such knowledge for us.
C) Because we need more proofs.
D) Because we are not rational enough.

Key Takeaway
God's existence is the most manifest reality, but His essence is known only to Him; we are given sufficient knowledge for worship.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You claim to believe that God's existence is the most manifest reality. But if you were silenced today, would your life—your habits, priorities, and fears—declare that truth as clearly as the 'tongue of state'? What one change would make your life a more honest declaration of His existence?
?
The passage reminds you that you were born knowing nothing. What areas of your faith have you become arrogant in, pretending to understand more than God has revealed? Will you surrender that false certainty today and ask Him to teach you what you truly need?
?
If God's essence is hidden and beyond your grasp, then your worship must be based on what He has taught you—not on your own imagination. Are there any ways you have been worshipping a god of your own making rather than the God who revealed Himself through the proofs and the messengers? What will you change starting now?

Divine Transcendence
beginner

Dismissing Imaginary Objections to Definitive Beliefs
Sanusi dismisses imaginary objections and asserts the limitation of human intellect before divine transcendence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that definitive proofs of faith should not be challenged by imagination, and that this topic is beyond rational objection.

Core Idea
Imagination cannot challenge definitive proofs.

Sanusi concludes with a powerful dismissal of any objection from imagination against the necessary beliefs established by definitive proofs. He warns against overstepping one's capacity and reminds that even great scholars have fallen short in comprehending divine transcendence. This lesson captures that final exhortation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Notice the strong command 'اخسأ' (Begone) and the reference to capacity.
This is a direct address to the faculty of imagination.
2
Identify the type of beliefs involved
Sanusi refers to beliefs known necessarily (darura) through definitive proofs (barahin qati'a). These are sure truths of faith.
Imagination cannot compete with definitive proofs.
3
Understand the warning
Sanusi says this station (maqam) is not suitable for imagination, and only those specially guided can approach it.
The poetry that follows underscores the humility of even great imams.
4
Reflect on the poetry
The poet laments that after touring all institutes, he found only people astonished or remorseful, showing the inadequacy of human intellect before God's majesty.
This reinforces the lesson's core idea.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الجلال ، الذي لا يحصرُهُ حدّ ولا يُتَعَرَّفُ بمثالٍ ، ولم يعلم هذا المصغي أذنَهُ للوهم أنَّهُ ليسَ معَ هذا الوهم إلا عدم الشعور بذاتِ ليسَتْ بِجِرْمٍ ولا عَرَضٍ ، ولا يلزمُ مِنْ عدم الشعور بشيء عدم وجودِهِ ألم يعلم العاقلُ : بأنَّ ما اطَّلَعَ عليهِ مِنَ الأجرام والقائم بها ؛ لولا أنَّ الله تعالى فتح لهُ مِنَ العلم بهِ . لَمّا أدرك منه شيئاً ؟! بل لو لم يفتح لهُ في الشعورِ بذاتِهِ لَمَا شعرَ بها أصلاً ، ولينظر إلى الجمادات وإلى الحيوانات المماثلة له كيف تعذَّرَ عليها إدراك ما لم يفتح لها في إدراكه وإن كان واضحاً عند غيرها . جلال الذاتِ العليَّة في ظهورها وبطونها ] فالذات العلية وجودها مُحقَّق واجبٌ ، أظهرُ مِنْ كُلِّ ظاهرٍ ، وكلُّ جزء مِنْ أجزاء العالم وكلُّ صفةٍ مِنْ صفاتِهِ تلهج بذلك بلسان الحال وتُفصِحُ بهِ أبينَ وأوضحَ مِنْ إفصاح المقال ، لكن مع ذلكَ لا طريق إلى معرفة حقيقتها بما فتح لنا تعالى في إدراكه مِنْ حقائقِ الكائناتِ الحادثة ؛ إذ لا مثلَ لهُ تعالى منها جلَّ وعزَّ ، ولم يخلق تعالى لنا عِلْماً بحقيقةِ ذاتِهِ الواجبةِ الوجودِ ، كما لم يخلق تعالى للجماداتِ وكثيرٍ مِنَ الحيوانات إدراكاً بما هو مُحقَّقُ الوجودِ مِنْ أنفسها القريبة إليها جداً فما فوق ذلك ، ولا علم لأحدٍ مِنَ الكائناتِ إِلا بما علَّمَهُ لهُ مولاه جلَّ وعزَّ ، وفتح له فيه بفضلِهِ وقد فتح سبحانَهُ بفضلِهِ في معرفتِنا بوجودِهِ وصفاتِهِ على وجه تميَّزَ بهِ في عقولنا عن كل ما سواه ، وأعلمنا تعالى مِنَ البراهين ما عرفنا بهِ صدْقَ رُسُلِهِ على وجه عرفنا بهِ أحكامه المتوجهة إلينا ، وما وراء ذلكَ لا تتوقَّفُ عليهِ عبادة مولانا جل وعزَّ ولا إخلاص العبوديَّةِ لهُ تعالى ، ونحن عاجزون عن إدراكه إلا أن يتفضَّلَ سبحانه وتعالى بما يشاءُ مِنَ الإدراكِ بعد ، كما كنا عاجزينَ في أصل نشأتنا عن كل إدراك حتى تفضَّلَ سبحانَهُ بما شاءَ ، لهُ الحمدُ جلَّ وعلا كما يليقُ بهِ ، أَخْرَجَكُم مِّنْ بُطُونِ أُمَّهَيْكُمْ لَا تَعْلَمُونَ شَيْئًا) [النحل : ٧٨] . ومهما اعترضنا الوهم الغبيُّ الكاذبُ فيما عرفناه ضرورةً مِنَ العقائدِ بالبراهين القطعيَّة الصادقة .. قلنا له : اخسأ ، فلن تعدو قدرك (١) ، وليس هذا مقاماً يصلحُ لك حتى تُعلَّقَ بهِ سَرَّكَ ، فلا تتطاول إلى الحديثِ فيهِ ، وإنَّما هذا مقام لا يهتدي إليه إلا المعتنى بهِ ، الشريف الموفَّقُ مِنَ العقولِ ، وكم انقطع دونَ فِيحِ صحرائِهِ مِنَ الأَئِمَّةِ الفحول . لَعَمْرِي لَقَدْ طُفْتُ الْمَعَاهِدَ كُلَّهَا وَسَرَّحْتُ طَرْفِي بَيْنَ تِلْكَ الْمَعَالِمِ فَلَمْ أَرَ إِلا وَاضِعاً كَفَّ حَائِرٍ عَلَى ذَقَنِ أَوْ قَارِعاً سِنَّ نَادِمِ (٢)
The Majesty, which no limit confines nor is known by a likeness, and this one who lends his ear to imagination (al-wahm) does not know that with this imagination there is only lack of perception of an essence that is not a body nor an accident. And it does not follow from lack of perception of something its non-existence. Does not the rational person know that what he has observed of bodies and what subsists in them – if God had not opened for him knowledge of it, he would not have perceived anything of it? Indeed, if He had not opened for him perception of his own self, he would not have perceived it at all. And let him look at inanimate objects and animals similar to him how it was impossible for them to perceive what He did not open for them to perceive, even if it is clear to others. The majesty of the high essence in its manifestation and hiddenness. So the high essence: its existence is realized, necessary, more manifest than any manifest thing, and every part of the world and every attribute of it speaks of that in the tongue of state and makes it clear more clearly and plainly than the clarity of speech. But despite that, there is no way to know its reality through what He has opened to us in perceiving the realities of created beings; for there is no likeness to Him from them, exalted and mighty. And He did not create for us knowledge of the reality of His necessarily existent essence, just as He did not create for inanimate objects and many animals perception of what is realized in existence from their own selves that are very close to them, and beyond that. And there is no knowledge for any of the created beings except what his Master taught him and opened for him in it by His grace. And He has opened by His grace to our knowledge of His existence and attributes in a way that distinguishes Him in our minds from everything else. And He taught us from the proofs (al-barahin) what we know by it the truth of His messengers in a way that we know by it His laws directed to us. And what is beyond that, worship of our Master and sincerity of servitude to Him does not depend on it. And we are incapable of perceiving it unless He bestows as He wills from perception afterwards, just as we were incapable at the origin of our creation from all perception until He bestowed as He willed. To Him is praise, exalted and high, as befits Him. "He brought you out from the wombs of your mothers knowing nothing" [an-Nahl 16:78]. And whenever the stupid false imagination objects to us in what we know necessarily of beliefs by truthful definitive proofs, we say to it: "Begone, you will not exceed your capacity" (1), and this is not a place suitable for you to attach your secret to it. So do not stretch forward to speak in it. And this is a station that only the one who is cared for, the noble, the divinely guided intellects can find guidance to. And how many of the great imams have fallen short before the vastness of its desert. By my life, I have toured all the institutes and let my eye wander among those landmarks, and I saw only one placing a hand of astonishment on his chin or one gnashing the tooth of remorse. (2)
Source pages p. 249

Commentary
This passage is a multifaceted argument affirming the transcendence of God's essence and the epistemological limits of created beings. It begins by addressing a common objection from the estimative faculty (wahm): that if we do not perceive something, it does not exist. The author refutes this by noting that perception itself is a gift from God; we do not even perceive our own selves without His opening. He draws an analogy to inanimate objects and animals, which cannot perceive what is obvious to others, underscoring that lack of perception does not entail non-existence. 

Then follows a heading: 'The majesty of the high essence in its manifestation and hiddenness.' The author affirms that God's existence is necessary and more manifest than anything else; all of creation declares His existence in the 'tongue of state' more clearly than speech. Yet, despite this manifestness, we cannot know His reality (haqiqa) through created things because He has no likeness. 

The argument continues: God has not given us knowledge of the reality of His essence, just as He did not give animals knowledge of their own existence. All knowledge is solely by God's teaching and favor. What He has granted us is knowledge of His existence and attributes, enough to distinguish Him from all else, and proofs to verify the truth of His messengers and His revealed laws. Knowledge beyond this is not required for worship and sincerity of servitude. We are incapable of such perception unless God grants it, as He granted us perception from total ignorance at birth, as the Quranic verse states: 'He brought you out from the wombs of your mothers knowing nothing.'

Finally, the author dismisses any objection from a 'stupid false imagination' against the necessary beliefs known through definitive proofs. He quotes a hadith: 'Begone, you will not exceed your capacity,' and declares that this subject is too lofty for such objections; only divinely guided intellects can approach it. The passage concludes with two lines of poetry by al-Shahrastani, lamenting how many great scholars have fallen short before this vast topic.

Key Terms
الوهم
براهين قطعية
مقام

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That rational imagination can legitimately object to the definitive proofs of faith.
Correction: Sanusi teaches that imagination is inherently limited and must be silenced when it tries to challenge what is known necessarily through definitive proofs.

Checkpoint
What does Sanusi command when imagination objects to definitive beliefs?
A) 'Explain yourself'
B) 'Begone, you will not exceed your capacity'
C) 'Prove your argument'
D) 'Submit to reason'

Key Takeaway
Definitive proofs of faith are beyond the reach of imagination; we must humbly accept our limits.

How often do you find yourself feeling intellectually superior in matters of faith, thinking you can figure it out on your own? Reflect on the poetry: even great scholars are left bewildered. Where do you stand?
?
What imaginary objection have you been nursing against a definitive teaching of Islam? Will you now 'command it to begone' and submit to the proof?

Divine Transcendence
beginner
